133359vidarBaThe modern Berār, a great kingdom in ancient times lying to the north of Kuntala and extending from the banks of the Kṛṣṇā to about the banks of the Narmadā. On account of its great size, the country was also called ‘Mahārāṣṭra’; Kuṇḍinapura, also called Vidarbhā, was its ancient capital, which probably stands for the modern Beder. The river Varadā (Warda) divided Vidarbha into two parts, Amarāvatī being the capital of the northern, and Pratiṣṭhāna of the southern, part.0.1950.129214012vidarBa ‘destitute of Darbha grass’, Name (also = title or epithet) of a country south of the Vindhya hills (now called Berar; it was the country of Damayantī, wife of Nala; the soil was probably grassless and arid, but the absence of Darbha is said to be due to the fact that the son of a saint died of the prick of a sharp blade of that grass), ; &c.0.1840.101214012vidarBa ‘destitute of Darbha grass’, Name (also = title or epithet) of a country south of the Vindhya hills (now called Berar; it was the country of Damayantī, wife of Nala; the soil was probably grassless and arid, but the absence of Darbha is said to be due to the fact that the son of a saint died of the prick of a sharp blade of that grass), ; &c.214012D

133361videhaof a country lying to the north-east of Magadha. Its capital Mithilā is the same as Janakapur in Nepal north of Madhuvāṇī.
